    "# Introduction\n",
    "\n",
    "My name is Vijay Sudharshan and I like Pokemon. I got into Pokemon as a child and loved the movies and games and TV series that were all a part of the franchise. However, I only recently got into the video game series as they were a little convoluted for me as a child. The Pokemon video game franchise is one of the most popular to date and has it's own professional tournaments that you can compete in. Nintendo reinvigorated the game by releasing Pokemon Go in collaboration with Niantic which has its own version of Pokemon battles. In this tutorial, I shall come up with an algorithm to find the best 10 pokemon to beat a given pokemon using their stats and moves. I shall analyze the data primarily using dataframes that can be The Pokemon I want to beat are the top tier Pokemon according to http://www.eurogamer.net/articles/2017-12-15-pokemon-go-best-pokemon-highest-hp-attack-defence-stats. The dataset I shall use is from Kaggle which was a resource recommended by our professors: https://www.kaggle.com/abcsds/pokemon"
   ]

   "source": [
    "So here we have the dataset which lists all 721 pokemon and their individual stats, type(s), generation, and whether they are legendary or not. You can use any Pokemon from the first 251 to battle each other as those are the only ones currently available in the game. In the future, as the developers add more Pokemon to the game, I can simply change the size of the dataset and continue through the tutorial.\n",
    "\n",
    "Contrary to popular belief, the best team does not just consist of the Pokemon with the best stats. The Pokemon's type and move set also play a large role in which Pokemon will win. For example, Pokemon A might have a more powerful attack, but if Pokemon B has a higher defense and speed, then it will likely defeat A.  Since we don't have a pokemon's moveset included in the dataset, let's try to scrape that data from the web."
   ]
  },

   "cell_type": "code",

       "[251]"

   ],
   "source": [
    "url='http://www.eurogamer.net/articles/2017-11-06-pokemon-go-moves-movesets-move-list-and-highest-dps-attacks'\n",
    "page = requests.get(url)\n",
    "doc = lh.fromstring(page.content)\n",
    "tbody_elements = doc.xpath('//tbody')\n",
    "num_pokemon = [len(T) for T in tbody_elements[:1]]\n",
    "num_pokemon"
   ]

    "pkmn_copy = pokemon\n",
    "pokemon = pokemon.drop_duplicates(subset=['#'], keep=\"first\")\n",
    "pokemon = pokemon.reset_index(drop=True)\n",
    "firstandsecondgen = pokemon.head(n=251)\n",
    "\n",
    "frames = [firstandsecondgen,moveset]\n",
    "pkmn = pd.concat(frames, axis=1)\n",
    "pkmn = pkmn.drop([\"#s\"],axis=1)\n",
    "pkmn_stats = pkmn.drop([\"#\",\"Moves\",\"Generation\"],axis=1)\n",
    "pkmn_stats = pkmn_stats.drop([\"Legendary\"],axis=1)\n",
    "pkmn_stats = pkmn_stats.sort_index(ascending=True)\n",
    "\n",
    "#pkmn\n",
    "pkmn_stats"

   "source": [
    "We have reached the end of Part 1 where we end with two dataframes: one that contains all the information merged together and a smaller dataframe (displayed above) that only contains the stats of each Pokemon. To display one or the other, simply uncomment the line that is commented and comment out the one below it. In the next part, we shall tidy the data a bit in order to visually represent it."
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "## Part 2: Data Visualization"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "Generally, you want the fastest Pokemon with the strongest attack and strongest defense for it to be considered well rounded. Here is a quick explanation of all the various columns: \n",
    "\n",
    "#: ID for each Pokemon\n",
    "\n",
    "Name: Name of each Pokemon\n",
    "\n",
    "Type 1: Each Pokemon has a type, this determines weakness/resistance to attacks\n",
    "\n",
    "Type 2: 2nd type of Pokemon (will not be used in this tutorial!)\n",
    "\n",
    "Total: sum of all stats which gives a general idea of a Pokemon's overall strength\n",
    "\n",
    "HP: hit points, or health, defines how much damage a Pokemon can withstand before fainting\n",
    "\n",
    "Attack: the base modifier for normal attacks (eg. Scratch, Punch)\n",
    "\n",
    "Defense: the base damage resistance against normal attacks\n",
    "\n",
    "SP Atk: special attack, the base modifier for special attacks (e.g. fire blast, bubble beam)\n",
    "\n",
    "SP Def: the base damage resistance against special attacks\n",
    "\n",
    "Speed: determines which Pokemon attacks first each round\n",
    "\n",
    "In this section, I shall begin visualizing the data in order to get a better overall understanding of whether certain types of Pokemon are better than others. I'll start by tidying up the data in order to plot the the individual values of the stats."
   ]
  },

    "temp = pkmn_stats.drop([\"Total\"],axis=1)\n",
    "sns.boxplot(data=temp)\n",
    "plt.title('Value vs Stat')\n",
    "plt.show()\n",

   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "So we have 2 plots shown above. The first one is a boxplot that shows the overall distribution of individual stats of all the Pokemon which is useful as it shows us the min, max, and mean in each category. By eyeballing this plot you can see means for all the categories seem to be around 70 which can be verified by using the dataframe.describe() function. This is valuable information as it shows us that there are a lot of pokemon that are not viable options when trying to defeat the Top Tier Pokemon. So for this reason, we can use the mean total value of all the stats and create a filter to only consider Pokemon with a certain total value.\n",
    "\n",
    "The second plot is a scatterplot that shows a breakdown of Pokemon type in each category. This gives us a much more detailed view of what the boxplot showed as it shows that certain pokemon are better in certain categories. For example, here we can see that Electric pokemon tend to have the lowest HP of all the different types but tend to fare better in the Speed stat. This gives us a rudimentary understanding of which Pokemon will win in a certain category based on its type."
   ]

    "So I'll round down the mean to 67 and multiply that by 6 to get a mean total of 402 which will now be used as the cutoff for Pokemon I am looking for. As I mentioned previously, a Pokemon with the highest total is not always the best for the job. This is where the type of Pokemon comes into play. So to quickly summarize, certain types of Pokemon are more effective against others. They largely follow some basic natural law principles like water is 2x effective against fire and electricity is completely ineffective against ground types. To read more about which types are most effective against each other click http://www.eurogamer.net/articles/2017-12-15-pokemon-go-type-chart-effectiveness-weaknesses. Because of this, I will add the stat multipliers for each Pokemon to show how effective it will be against a Pokemon of a different type and its own type. "
   ]

   "source": [
    "# Top Tier Pokemon: Dragonite, Tyranitar, Blissey, Machamp, Vaporeon, Heracross, Jolteon, Snorlax, Lapras, Exeggutor\n",
    "# replace pk1 = 'X' with any of the above Pokemon\n",
    "pk1 = \"Vaporeon\"\n",
    "\n",
    "opponent_type = pkmn_trimmed[pkmn_trimmed['Name'] == pk1]['Type 1'].iloc[0]\n",
    "opponent_multiplier = pkmn_trimmed[opponent_type]\n",
    "adjusted_attack = pkmn_trimmed['Attack'] * opponent_multiplier\n",
    "adjusted_defense = pkmn_trimmed['Defense'] * opponent_multiplier\n",
    "adjusted_spAtk = pkmn_trimmed['Sp. Atk'] * opponent_multiplier\n",
    "adjusted_spDef = pkmn_trimmed['Sp. Def'] * opponent_multiplier\n",
    "adjusted_Speed = pkmn_trimmed['Speed'] * opponent_multiplier\n",
    "\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Attack'] = (adjusted_attack - adjusted_attack.min()) / (adjusted_attack.max() - adjusted_attack.min()) * 100\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Defense'] = (adjusted_defense - adjusted_defense.min()) / (adjusted_defense.max() - adjusted_defense.min()) * 100\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Sp. Atk'] = (adjusted_spAtk - adjusted_spAtk.min()) / (adjusted_spAtk.max() - adjusted_spAtk.min()) * 100\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Sp. Def'] = (adjusted_spDef - adjusted_spDef.min()) / (adjusted_spDef.max() - adjusted_spDef.min()) * 100\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Speed'] = (adjusted_Speed - adjusted_Speed.min()) / (adjusted_Speed.max() - adjusted_Speed.min()) * 100\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Total'] = pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Attack'] + pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Defense'] + pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Sp. Atk'] + pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Sp. Def'] + pkmn_trimmed['Adjusted Speed']\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed = pkmn_trimmed.sort_index(ascending=True)\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "Below is the completed algorithm to find out which are the best 10 Pokemon to attack the Top Tier Pokemon. The algorithm compiles a list of 10 Pokemon that are the best in attack, defense, etc. and then counts the number of occurrences of a Pokemon's name in the list and outputs that list in descending order. Some Pokemon may appear an equal number of times as each other which indicates that they are equally good at fighting the Top Tier Pokemon. "
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",

    "# For each adjusted value, find the best Pokemon in that category and append to a list.\n",
    "# Then output the list sorted by the Pokemon that appears the most meaning that it was \n",
    "# the best for that category (i.e. Adjusted Defense, etc.).\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed.sort_values('Adjusted Attack', inplace=True,ascending=False)\n",
    "best_10_attack = pkmn_trimmed.head(n=10)\n",
    "temp = []\n",
    "for item in best_10_attack.Name:\n",
    "    temp.append(item)\n",
    "      \n",
    "pkmn_trimmed.sort_values('Adjusted Defense', inplace=True,ascending=False)\n",
    "best_10_attack = pkmn_trimmed.head(n=10)\n",
    "for item in best_10_attack.Name:\n",
    "    temp.append(item)\n",
    "    \n",
    "pkmn_trimmed.sort_values('Adjusted Sp. Atk', inplace=True,ascending=False)\n",
    "best_10_attack = pkmn_trimmed.head(n=10)\n",
    "for item in best_10_attack.Name:\n",
    "    temp.append(item)\n",
    "    \n",
    "pkmn_trimmed.sort_values('Adjusted Sp. Def', inplace=True,ascending=False)\n",
    "best_10_attack = pkmn_trimmed.head(n=10)\n",
    "for item in best_10_attack.Name:\n",
    "    temp.append(item)\n",
    "\n",
    "pkmn_trimmed.sort_values('Adjusted Speed', inplace=True,ascending=False)\n",
    "best_10_attack = pkmn_trimmed.head(n=10)\n",
    "for item in best_10_attack.Name:\n",
    "    temp.append(item)\n",
    "    \n",
    "pkmn_trimmed.sort_values('Adjusted Total', inplace=True,ascending=False)\n",
    "best_10_attack = pkmn_trimmed.head(n=10)\n",
    "for item in best_10_attack.Name:\n",
    "    temp.append(item)\n",

To make things a little more interesting, I will use a Pokemon that does not appear on the online list but does in my output. This will either prove my algorithm is correct or needs to be improved."

    "pk2 = 'Bellossom'\n",
    "pk1_speed = pkmn_trimmed[pkmn_trimmed['Name'] == pk1]['Adjusted Speed'].iloc[0]\n",
    "pk2_speed = pkmn_trimmed[pkmn_trimmed['Name'] == pk2]['Adjusted Speed'].iloc[0]\n",
    "pk1_hp = pkmn_trimmed[pkmn_trimmed['Name'] == pk2]['HP'].iloc[0]\n",
    "pk2_hp = pkmn_trimmed[pkmn_trimmed['Name'] == pk2]['HP'].iloc[0]\n",
    "print(pk1, pkmn[pkmn['Name'] == pk1]['Moves'].iloc[0], pk1_speed)\n",
    "print(pk2, pkmn[pkmn['Name'] == pk2]['Moves'].iloc[0], pk2_speed)"

    "while pk1_hp>0 or pk2_hp>0:\n",
    "    if pk1_speed > pk2_speed:\n",
    "        pk2_hp = pk2_hp - 39.39\n",
    "        print('pk2_hp: ',pk2_hp)\n",
    "        if(pk2_hp < 0):\n",
    "            print(pk1, 'Wins!')\n",
    "            break\n",
    "        else:\n",
    "            pk1_hp = pk1_hp - 42.31\n",
    "            print('pk1_hp: ',pk1_hp)\n",
    "    else:\n",
    "        pk1_hp = pk1_hp - 42.31\n",
    "        print('pk1_hp: ',pk1_hp)\n",
    "        if(pk1_hp < 0):\n",
    "            print(pk2, 'Wins!')\n",
    "            break\n",

  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "The code block above is the simulated battle that would take place between the two Pokemon. Here's how it works. First I take into account the adjusted speed value and if the Pokemon from my list has a higher value then it gets to attack first and then the Top Tier Pokemon gets to attack. So for each time an attack occurs, the Pokemons' HP decreases and once a Pokemon's HP reaches 0 it has fainted is no longer able to battle. Assuming that both Pokemon will use their strongest moves against each other each round, I used those values as the attack values to subtract from the HP. So this shows that my algorithm indeed does work and that all the candidates presented from the algorithm are suitable to defeat the Top Tier Pokemon."
   ]
